<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Civic_administration">Civic administration</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neighbourhoods_of_Delhi" title="Neighbourhoods of Delhi">Neighbourhoods of Delhi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Districts_of_Delhi" title="Districts of Delhi">Districts of Delhi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_towns_in_National_Capital_Territory_of_Delhi" title="List of towns in National Capital Territory of Delhi">List of towns in National Capital Territory of Delhi</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dehli_districts.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="896" data-file-width="1231" decoding="async" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Dehli_districts.png/330px-Dehli_districts.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Dehli_districts.png/495px-Dehli_districts.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Dehli_districts.png/660px-Dehli_districts.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dehli_districts.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Districts of Delhi</div></div></div>
<p>Currently, the National Capital Territory of Delhi is made up of one division, <a href="/wiki/List_of_districts_of_Delhi" title="List of districts of Delhi">11 districts</a>, 33 subdivisions, 59 census towns, and 300 villages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup>
</p><p>The National Capital Territory of Delhi is divided into three municipalities, Delhi Municipality, New Delhi and Delhi Cantonment, each with their own governance apparatus. The Municipality of Delhi is administered by <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Corporation_of_Delhi" title="Municipal Corporation of Delhi">Municipal Corporation of Delhi</a> (MCD) which occupies an area of 1397.3 km<sup>2</sup> and is sub-divided into 12 zones, that is, Centre, South, West, Najafgarh, Rohini, Civil Lines, Karol Bagh, SP-City, Keshavpuram, Narela, Shahdara North and Shahdara South.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcdonline_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-mcdonline-134">[133]</a></sup> Municipal services in <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi" title="New Delhi">New Delhi</a>, which occupies an area of 42.7 km<sup>2</sup>, are provided by the <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi_Municipal_Council" title="New Delhi Municipal Council">New Delhi Municipal Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Cantonment" title="Delhi Cantonment">Delhi Cantonment</a> is administered by a <a href="/wiki/Cantonment_board" title="Cantonment board">Cantonment board</a>.
</p><p>Between 2011 and 22 May 2022 Delhi Municipality was divided into three municipal corporations:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup>
</p>
<ol><li><a href="/wiki/South_Delhi_Municipal_Corporation" title="South Delhi Municipal Corporation">South Delhi</a> had jurisdiction over South and West Delhi areas including Mahipalpur, Rajouri Garden, Badarpur, Jaitpur, Janakpuri, Hari Nagar, Tilak Nagar, Dwarka, Jungpura, Greater Kailash, R K Puram, Malviya Nagar, Kalkaji, Ambedkar Nagar and Pul pehladpur.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/North_Delhi_Municipal_Corporation" title="North Delhi Municipal Corporation">North Delhi</a> had jurisdiction over areas such as Badli, Rithala, Bawana, Kirari, Mangolpuri, Tri Nagar, Model Town, Sadar Bazar, Chandni Chowk, Matia Mahal, Karol Bagh, Moti Nagar</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/East_Delhi_Municipal_Corporation" title="East Delhi Municipal Corporation">East Delhi</a> had jurisdiction over areas such as Patparganj, Kondli, Laxmi Nagar, Seemapuri, Gonda, Karawal Nagar, Babarpur and Shahadra.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup></li></ol>
<p>Delhi is home to the <a href="/wiki/Delhi_High_Court" title="Delhi High Court">High Court of Delhi</a>. The High Court of Delhi is the highest in the Delhi before Supreme Court. The High Court of Delhi just like the apex court and other High Courts in India is the Court of record.   Delhi is also home to various District Court according to jurisdictions. Delhi have Currently seven District Courts namely Tis Hazari Court Complex,  Karkardooma Court Complex, Patiala House Court Complex, Rohini Court Complex, Dwarka Courts Complex, Saket Court Complex, and Rouse Avenue Court 
Apart from the District Courts Delhi also have Consumer Courts, CBI Courts, Labour Courts, Revenue Courts, Army tribunals, electricity tribunals, Railway Tribunals, and other various tribunals situated according to appropriate jurisdictions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup>
</p><p>For policing purposes Delhi is divided into fifteen <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Delhi_Police" title="Districts of Delhi Police">police districts</a> which are further subdivided into 95 local police station zones. Delhi currently has 180 police stations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-policestations_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-policestations-139">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Delhi" title="Government of Delhi">Government of Delhi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:392px;max-width:392px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:251px;max-width:251px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:202px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arvind_Kejriwal_smiling_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="784" decoding="async" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Arvind_Kejriwal_smiling_%28cropped%29.jpg/249px-Arvind_Kejriwal_smiling_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Arvind_Kejriwal_smiling_%28cropped%29.jpg/374px-Arvind_Kejriwal_smiling_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Arvind_Kejriwal_smiling_%28cropped%29.jpg/498px-Arvind_Kejriwal_smiling_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="249"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center"><a href="/wiki/Arvind_Kejriwal" title="Arvind Kejriwal">Arvind Kejriwal</a> is the seventh and current <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_of_Delhi" title="Chief Minister of Delhi">Chief Minister of Delhi</a>, first elected in February 2015.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:137px;max-width:137px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:202px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Delhi_Vidhan_Sabha.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Delhi_Vidhan_Sabha.jpg/135px-Delhi_Vidhan_Sabha.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Delhi_Vidhan_Sabha.jpg/203px-Delhi_Vidhan_Sabha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Delhi_Vidhan_Sabha.jpg/270px-Delhi_Vidhan_Sabha.jpg 2x" width="135"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center"><a href="/wiki/Delhi_Legislative_Assembly" title="Delhi Legislative Assembly">Delhi Legislative Assembly</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>As a first-level administrative division, the National Capital Territory of Delhi has its own <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Delhi" title="Legislative Assembly of Delhi">Legislative Assembly</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_lieutenant_governors_of_Delhi" title="List of lieutenant governors of Delhi">Lieutenant Governor</a>, the council of ministers, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_of_Delhi" title="Chief Minister of Delhi">Chief Minister</a>. Members of the legislative assembly are directly elected from territorial constituencies in the NCT. The legislative assembly was abolished in 1956, after which direct federal control was implemented until it was re-established in 1993. The Municipal corporation handles civic administration for the city as part of the Panchayati Raj Act. The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Delhi" title="Government of Delhi">Government of National Capital Territory of Delhi</a> jointly administer New Delhi, where both bodies are located. The <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_India" title="Parliament of India">Parliament of India</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rashtrapati_Bhavan" title="Rashtrapati Bhavan">Rashtrapati Bhavan</a> (Presidential Palace), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cabinet_Secretariat_of_India" title="Cabinet Secretariat of India">Cabinet Secretariat</a>, and the Supreme Court of India are located in the municipal district of New Delhi. There are 70 assembly constituencies and seven <a href="/wiki/Lok_Sabha" title="Lok Sabha">Lok Sabha</a> (Indian parliament's lower house) constituencies in Delhi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-assmbconst_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-assmbconst-141">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-loksabhaconst_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-loksabhaconst-142">[141]</a></sup>
The <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Indian National Congress</a> (Congress) formed all the governments in Delhi until the 1990s, when the <a href="/wiki/Bharatiya_Janata_Party" title="Bharatiya Janata Party">Bharatiya Janata Party</a> (BJP), led by <a href="/wiki/Madan_Lal_Khurana" title="Madan Lal Khurana">Madan Lal Khurana</a>, came to power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-POD_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-POD-143">[142]</a></sup> In 1998, the Congress returned to power under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Sheila_Dikshit" title="Sheila Dikshit">Sheila Dikshit</a>, who was subsequently re-elected for 3 consecutive terms. But in <a href="/wiki/2013_Delhi_Legislative_Assembly_election" title="2013 Delhi Legislative Assembly election">2013</a>, the Congress was ousted from power by the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Aam_Aadmi_Party" title="Aam Aadmi Party">Aam Aadmi Party</a> (AAP) led by <a href="/wiki/Arvind_Kejriwal" title="Arvind Kejriwal">Arvind Kejriwal</a> forming the government with outside support from the Congress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> However, that government was short-lived, collapsing only after 49 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup> Delhi was then under <a href="/wiki/President%27s_rule" title="President's rule">President's rule</a> until February 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> On 10 February 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Aam_Aadmi_Party" title="Aam Aadmi Party">Aam Aadmi Party</a> returned to power after a landslide victory, winning 67 out of the 70 seats in the Delhi Legislative Assembly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Delhi" title="Economy of Delhi">Economy of Delhi</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:392px;max-width:392px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:119px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dry_fruits_being_sold_at_Khari_Baoli_market_in_Old_Delhi.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2598" data-file-width="3900" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Dry_fruits_being_sold_at_Khari_Baoli_market_in_Old_Delhi.jpg/180px-Dry_fruits_being_sold_at_Khari_Baoli_market_in_Old_Delhi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Dry_fruits_being_sold_at_Khari_Baoli_market_in_Old_Delhi.jpg/270px-Dry_fruits_being_sold_at_Khari_Baoli_market_in_Old_Delhi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Dry_fruits_being_sold_at_Khari_Baoli_market_in_Old_Delhi.jpg/360px-Dry_fruits_being_sold_at_Khari_Baoli_market_in_Old_Delhi.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">The <a href="/wiki/Khari_Baoli" title="Khari Baoli">Khari Baoli</a> market in Old Delhi is one of the oldest and busiest in the city.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:206px;max-width:206px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:119px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Connaught_Place_New_Delhi.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1485" data-file-width="2524" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Connaught_Place_New_Delhi.jpg/204px-Connaught_Place_New_Delhi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Connaught_Place_New_Delhi.jpg/306px-Connaught_Place_New_Delhi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Connaught_Place_New_Delhi.jpg/408px-Connaught_Place_New_Delhi.jpg 2x" width="204"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center"><a href="/wiki/Connaught_Place,_New_Delhi" title="Connaught Place, New Delhi">Connaught Place</a> in New Delhi is an important economic hub of the <a href="/wiki/National_Capital_Region_(India)" title="National Capital Region (India)">National Capital Region</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Delhi is the largest commercial center in northern India. As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Delhi&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> recent estimates of the economy of the Delhi urban area have been around $370 billion (<a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP</a> <a href="/wiki/Gross_metropolitan_product" title="Gross metropolitan product">metro GDP</a>) ranking it either the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP" title="List of cities by GDP">most or second-most productive metro area</a> of India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gdp_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-gdp-148">[147]</a></sup> The nominal <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indian_states_and_union_territories_by_GDP" title="List of Indian states and union territories by GDP">GSDP</a> of the NCT of Delhi for 2016–17 was estimated at <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>6,224 billion</span> (US$78 billion), 13% higher than in 2015–16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Budget_Analysis_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-Budget_Analysis-149">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metrogdp_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-metrogdp-150">[149]</a></sup>
As per the Economic survey of Delhi (2005–2006), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_industry" title="Tertiary sector of industry">tertiary sector</a> contributes 70.95% of Delhi's gross SDP followed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secondary_sector_of_industry" title="Secondary sector of industry">secondary</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_sector_of_industry" title="Primary sector of industry">primary</a> sectors with 25.20% and 3.85% contributions, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecosurv2_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-ecosurv2-151">[150]</a></sup> Delhi's workforce constitutes 32.82% of the population, and increased by 52.52% between 1991 and 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecosurv5_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-ecosurv5-152">[151]</a></sup> Delhi's unemployment rate decreased from 12.57% in 1999–2000 to 4.63% in 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecosurv5_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-ecosurv5-152">[151]</a></sup> In December 2004, 636,000 people were registered with various employment exchange programmes in Delhi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecosurv5_152-2"><a href="#cite_note-ecosurv5-152">[151]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2001 the total workforce in national and state governments and the quasi-government sector was 620,000, and the private sector employed 219,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecosurv5_152-3"><a href="#cite_note-ecosurv5-152">[151]</a></sup> Key service industries are information technology, telecommunications, hotels, banking, media and tourism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup> Construction, power, health and community services and real estate are also important to the city's economy. Delhi has one of India's largest and fastest growing retail industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup> Manufacturing also grew considerably as consumer goods companies established manufacturing units and headquarters in the city. Delhi's large consumer market and the availability of skilled labour has also attracted foreign investment. In 2001, the manufacturing sector employed 1,440,000 workers and the city had 129,000 industrial units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecosurv9_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-ecosurv9-155">[154]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Utility_services">Utility services</span></h2>
<p>Delhi's municipal water supply is managed by the <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Jal_Board" title="Delhi Jal Board">Delhi Jal Board</a> (DJB). As of June 2005<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Delhi&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it supplied 650 million gallons per day (MGD), whereas the estimated consumption requirement is 963 MGD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecosurv13_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-ecosurv13-156">[155]</a></sup> The shortfall is met by private and public <a href="/wiki/Tube_well" title="Tube well">tube wells</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hand_pump" title="Hand pump">hand pumps</a>. At 240 MGD, the Bhakra storage is DJB's largest water source, followed by the Yamuna and <a href="/wiki/Ganges" title="Ganges">Ganges</a> rivers. Delhi's <a href="/wiki/Groundwater" title="Groundwater">groundwater</a> level is falling and its population density is increasing, so residents often encounter acute water shortage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecosurv13_156-1"><a href="#cite_note-ecosurv13-156">[155]</a></sup> Research on Delhi suggests that up to half of the city's water use is unofficial groundwater.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup><br/>In Delhi, daily domestic solid waste production is 8000 <a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">tonnes</a> which is dumped at three <a href="/wiki/Landfill" title="Landfill">landfill</a> locations by MCD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hinduwaste_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-hinduwaste-158">[157]</a></sup> The daily domestic waste water production is 470 MGD and industrial waste water is 70 MGD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Delhirisks_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-Delhirisks-159">[158]</a></sup> A large portion of the sewage flows untreated into the Yamuna river.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Delhirisks_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-Delhirisks-159">[158]</a></sup>
</p><p>The city's electricity consumption is about 1,265 kWh per capita but the actual demand is higher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecosurv11_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-ecosurv11-160">[159]</a></sup> In Delhi power distribution is managed by <a href="/wiki/Tata_Power_Delhi_Distribution_Limited" title="Tata Power Delhi Distribution Limited">TPDDL</a> and <a href="/wiki/BSES_Yamuna_Power_Limited" title="BSES Yamuna Power Limited">BSES Yamuna</a> &amp; BSES Rajdhani since 2002. The <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Fire_Service" title="Delhi Fire Service">Delhi Fire Service</a> runs 43 fire stations that attend about 15,000 fire and rescue calls per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dfs_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-dfs-161">[160]</a></sup> The state-owned <a href="/wiki/Bharat_Sanchar_Nigam_Limited" title="Bharat Sanchar Nigam Limited">BSNL</a> and private enterprises such as <a href="/wiki/Bharti_Airtel" title="Bharti Airtel">Airtel</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vodafone_Idea" title="Vodafone Idea">Vi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jio" title="Jio">Jio</a>, and provide telephone and cell phone services to the city. Cellular coverage is available in <a href="/wiki/GSM" title="GSM">GSM</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CDMA" title="CDMA">CDMA</a>, <a href="/wiki/3G" title="3G">3G</a>, <a href="/wiki/4G" title="4G">4G</a> and <a href="/wiki/LTE_Advanced" title="LTE Advanced">4G+</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Delhi" title="Transport in Delhi">Transport in Delhi</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mudras_at_Indira_Gandhi_Delhi_1007.jpg"><img alt="Shown here is the check-in counter at Terminal 3 of the airport." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Mudras_at_Indira_Gandhi_Delhi_1007.jpg/220px-Mudras_at_Indira_Gandhi_Delhi_1007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Mudras_at_Indira_Gandhi_Delhi_1007.jpg/330px-Mudras_at_Indira_Gandhi_Delhi_1007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Mudras_at_Indira_Gandhi_Delhi_1007.jpg/440px-Mudras_at_Indira_Gandhi_Delhi_1007.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mudras_at_Indira_Gandhi_Delhi_1007.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi_International_Airport" title="Indira Gandhi International Airport">Indira Gandhi International Airport</a>'s immigration counter in Terminal 3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[161]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi_International_Airport" title="Indira Gandhi International Airport">Indira Gandhi International Airport</a>, situated to the south-west of Delhi, is the main gateway for the city's domestic and international civilian air traffic. In 2015–16, the airport handled more than 48 million passengers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup> making it the busiest airport in India and South Asia. Terminal 3, which cost <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>96.8 billion</span> (US$1.2 billion) to construct between 2007 and 2010, handles an additional 37 million passengers annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup> In 2010, IGIA was conferred the 4th best airport award in the world in the 15–25 million category, by <a href="/wiki/Airports_Council_International" title="Airports Council International">Airports Council International</a>. The airport was rated as the <i>Best airport in the world</i> in the 25–40 million passengers category in 2015, by Airports Council International. Delhi Airport was awarded <i>The Best Airport in Central Asia</i> and <i>Best Airport Staff in Central Asia</i> at the <a href="/wiki/Skytrax" title="Skytrax">Skytrax</a> World Airport Awards 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hindon_Airport" title="Hindon Airport">Hindon Domestic Airport</a> in Ghaziabad was inaugurated by Prime Minister Narendra Modi as the second airport for the Delhi-NCR Region on 8 March 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup> A second international airport open for commercial flights has been suggested either by expansion of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meerut_Airport" title="Meerut Airport">Meerut Airport</a> or construction of a new airport in <a href="/wiki/Greater_Noida" title="Greater Noida">Greater Noida</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[167]</a></sup>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taj_International_Airport" title="Taj International Airport">Taj International Airport</a> project in <a href="/wiki/Jewar" title="Jewar">Jewar</a> has been approved by the <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a> government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <i>Delhi Flying Club</i>, established in 1928 with two <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Moth" title="De Havilland Moth">de Havilland Moth</a> aircraft named <i>Delhi</i> and <i>Roshanara</i>, was based at <a href="/wiki/Safdarjung_Airport" title="Safdarjung Airport">Safdarjung Airport</a> which started operations in 1929, when it was the Delhi's only airport and the second in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mecca_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-mecca-170">[169]</a></sup> The airport functioned until 2001; however, in January 2002 the government closed the airport for flying activities because of security concerns following <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/9/11" title="9/11">the New York attacks in September 2001</a>. Since then, the club only carries out aircraft maintenance courses and is used for helicopter rides to Indira Gandhi International Airport for VIP including the president and the prime minister.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mecca_170-1"><a href="#cite_note-mecca-170">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:392px;max-width:392px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:135px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Delhi_Metro_and_CNG_Buses_in_Azadpur_Neighborhood.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Delhi_Metro_and_CNG_Buses_in_Azadpur_Neighborhood.jpg/180px-Delhi_Metro_and_CNG_Buses_in_Azadpur_Neighborhood.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Delhi_Metro_and_CNG_Buses_in_Azadpur_Neighborhood.jpg/270px-Delhi_Metro_and_CNG_Buses_in_Azadpur_Neighborhood.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Delhi_Metro_and_CNG_Buses_in_Azadpur_Neighborhood.jpg/360px-Delhi_Metro_and_CNG_Buses_in_Azadpur_Neighborhood.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center"><a href="/wiki/Compressed_natural_gas" title="Compressed natural gas">Compressed natural gas</a> red- and green buses have low floors; orange has standard. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[b]</a></sup></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:206px;max-width:206px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:135px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Old_Delhi_rickshaw_2011.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Old_Delhi_rickshaw_2011.JPG/204px-Old_Delhi_rickshaw_2011.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Old_Delhi_rickshaw_2011.JPG/306px-Old_Delhi_rickshaw_2011.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Old_Delhi_rickshaw_2011.JPG/408px-Old_Delhi_rickshaw_2011.JPG 2x" width="204"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">The <a href="/wiki/Cycle_rickshaw" title="Cycle rickshaw">cycle rickshaw</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Auto_rickshaw" title="Auto rickshaw">auto rickshaw</a> are commonly used in Delhi for travelling short distances.</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Delhi has the highest road density of 2103 km/100 km<sup>2</sup> in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IND1_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-IND1-174">[172]</a></sup> It is connected to other parts of India by five <a href="/wiki/National_highways_of_India" title="National highways of India">National Highways</a>: <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_1_(India,_old_numbering)" title="National Highway 1 (India, old numbering)">NH 1</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_2_(India,_old_numbering)" title="National Highway 2 (India, old numbering)">NH 2</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_8_(India,_old_numbering)" title="National Highway 8 (India, old numbering)">NH 8</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_10_(India,_old_numbering)" title="National Highway 10 (India, old numbering)">NH 10</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_24_(India)" title="National Highway 24 (India)">NH 24</a>. The Delhi–Mumbai and Delhi–Kolkata prongs of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Quadrilateral" title="Golden Quadrilateral">Golden Quadrilateral</a> start from the city. The city's road network is maintained by MCD, NDMC, Delhi Cantonment Board, Public Works Department (PWD) and <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Development_Authority" title="Delhi Development Authority">Delhi Development Authority</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-roadauth_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-roadauth-175">[173]</a></sup>
</p><p>Buses are the most popular means of road transport catering to about 60% of Delhi's total demand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ET_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-ET-176">[174]</a></sup> Delhi has one of India's largest bus transport systems. In 1998, the Supreme Court of India ruled that all public transport vehicles in Delhi must be fuelled by <a href="/wiki/Compressed_natural_gas" title="Compressed natural gas">compressed natural gas</a> (CNG) to tackle increasing vehicular pollution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-supremelaw_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-supremelaw-177">[175]</a></sup> The state-owned <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Transport_Corporation" title="Delhi Transport Corporation">Delhi Transport Corporation</a> (DTC) is a major bus service provider which operates the world's largest fleet of CNG-fuelled buses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DTC_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-DTC-178">[176]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ND_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-ND-179">[177]</a></sup> In addition, cluster scheme buses are operated by <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Integrated_Multi-Modal_Transit_System" title="Delhi Integrated Multi-Modal Transit System">Delhi Integrated Multi-Modal Transit System</a> (DIMTS) with the participation of private concessionaires and DTC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[178]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[179]</a></sup> In December 2017, the DTC and cluster buses carried over 4.19 million passengers per day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maharana_Pratap_Inter_State_Bus_Terminus" title="Maharana Pratap Inter State Bus Terminus">Kashmiri Gate ISBT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swami_Vivekanand_Inter_State_Bus_Terminus" title="Swami Vivekanand Inter State Bus Terminus">Anand Vihar ISBT</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sarai_Kale_Khan_Inter-State_Bus_Terminus" title="Sarai Kale Khan Inter-State Bus Terminus">Sarai Kale Khan ISBT</a> are the main bus terminals for outstation buses plying to neighbouring states. Delhi's rapid rate of economic development and population growth has resulted in an increasing demand for transport, creating excessive pressure on the city's transport infrastructure. To meet the transport demand, the State and Union government constructed a mass rapid transit system, including the Delhi Metro.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecosurv12_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-ecosurv12-183">[181]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Bus_Rapid_Transit_System" title="Delhi Bus Rapid Transit System">Delhi Bus Rapid Transit System</a> runs between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ambedkar_Nagar" title="Ambedkar Nagar">Ambedkar Nagar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Gate,_Delhi" title="Delhi Gate, Delhi">Delhi Gate</a>.
</p><p>Personal vehicles especially cars also form a major chunk of vehicles plying on Delhi roads. As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Delhi&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, private vehicles account for 30% of the total demand for transport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecosurv12_183-1"><a href="#cite_note-ecosurv12-183">[181]</a></sup> Delhi has the highest number of registered cars compared to any other metropolitan city in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[182]</a></sup> Taxis, auto rickshaws, and cycle rickshaws also ply on Delhi roads in large numbers. As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Delhi&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the number of vehicles in the metropolitan region, Delhi NCR, was 11.2 million (11.2 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup> In 2008, there were 85 cars in Delhi for every 1,000 of its residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[184]</a></sup> In 2017, the number of vehicles in Delhi city alone crossed the ten million mark with the transport department of <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Delhi" title="Government of Delhi">Delhi Government</a> putting the total number of registered vehicles at 10,567,712 until 25 May of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[185]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway">Railway</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Delhi_railway_station_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1832" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/New_Delhi_railway_station_2.jpg/220px-New_Delhi_railway_station_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/New_Delhi_railway_station_2.jpg/330px-New_Delhi_railway_station_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/New_Delhi_railway_station_2.jpg/440px-New_Delhi_railway_station_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Delhi_railway_station_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A passenger train at the <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi_railway_station" title="New Delhi railway station">New Delhi railway station</a>. Freight awaits pick up or transportation to other destinations.</div></div></div>
<p>Delhi is a major junction in the Indian railway network and is the headquarters of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Railway_(India)" title="Northern Railway (India)">Northern Railway</a>. The main railway stations are <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi_railway_station" title="New Delhi railway station">New Delhi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delhi_Junction_Railway_Station" title="Delhi Junction Railway Station">Old Delhi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hazrat_Nizamuddin_Railway_Station" title="Hazrat Nizamuddin Railway Station">Hazrat Nizamuddin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anand_Vihar_Railway_Terminal" title="Anand Vihar Railway Terminal">Anand Vihar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Sarai_Rohilla_railway_station" title="Delhi Sarai Rohilla railway station">Delhi Sarai Rohilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Cantonment_railway_station" title="Delhi Cantonment railway station">Delhi Cantt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecosurv12_183-2"><a href="#cite_note-ecosurv12-183">[181]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Metro" title="Delhi Metro">Delhi Metro</a>, a mass rapid transit system built and operated by <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Metro_Rail_Corporation" title="Delhi Metro Rail Corporation">Delhi Metro Rail Corporation</a> (DMRC), serves many parts of Delhi and the neighbouring cities <a href="/wiki/Ghaziabad" title="Ghaziabad">Ghaziabad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faridabad" title="Faridabad">Faridabad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gurgaon" title="Gurgaon">Gurgaon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Noida" title="Noida">Noida</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup> As of December 2021<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Delhi&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the metro consists of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Delhi_Metro_lines" title="List of Delhi Metro lines">ten operational lines</a> with a total length of 348.12 km (216.31 mi) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Delhi_metro_stations" title="List of Delhi metro stations">254 stations</a>, and several other lines are under construction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tie-10aug18_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-tie-10aug18-189">[187]</a></sup> The Phase-I was built at a cost of US$2.3 billion and the Phase-II was expected to cost an additional <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>216 billion</span> (US$2.7 billion).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloomberg.com:_Opinion_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg.com:_Opinion-190">[188]</a></sup> Phase-II has a total length of 128 km and was completed by 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Economictimes.indiatimes.com_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-Economictimes.indiatimes.com-191">[189]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Metro" title="Delhi Metro">Delhi Metro</a> completed 10 years of operation on 25 December 2012. It carries millions of passengers every day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10_years_of_Delhi_Metro_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-10_years_of_Delhi_Metro-192">[190]</a></sup> In addition to the Delhi Metro, a suburban railway, the <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Suburban_Railway" title="Delhi Suburban Railway">Delhi Suburban Railway</a> exists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Indian_Express_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-Indian_Express-193">[191]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metro">Metro</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DelhiMetroBlueLineBombardier.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="5472" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/DelhiMetroBlueLineBombardier.jpg/220px-DelhiMetroBlueLineBombardier.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/DelhiMetroBlueLineBombardier.jpg/330px-DelhiMetroBlueLineBombardier.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/DelhiMetroBlueLineBombardier.jpg/440px-DelhiMetroBlueLineBombardier.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DelhiMetroBlueLineBombardier.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Delhi_Metro" title="Delhi Metro">Delhi Metro</a> is widely used in the <a href="/wiki/National_Capital_Region_(India)" title="National Capital Region (India)">NCR</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Metro" title="Delhi Metro">Delhi Metro</a> is a rapid transit system serving Delhi, <a href="/wiki/Ghaziabad" title="Ghaziabad">Ghaziabad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faridabad" title="Faridabad">Faridabad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gurgaon" title="Gurgaon">Gurgaon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Noida" title="Noida">Noida</a> in the National Capital Region of India. Delhi Metro is the world's tenth-largest metro system in terms of length. Delhi Metro was India's second modern public transportation system. The network consists of <a href="#Network">10 colour-coded lines</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-present_network_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-present_network-194">[192]</a></sup> serving <a href="/wiki/List_of_Delhi_Metro_stations" title="List of Delhi Metro stations">255 stations</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fn1_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-fn1-197">[c]</a></sup> with a total length of 348.12 kilometres (216.31 mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fn2_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-fn2-198">[d]</a></sup> The system has a mix of underground, at-grade, and elevated stations using both <a href="/wiki/Broad-gauge_railway" title="Broad-gauge railway">broad-gauge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Standard-gauge_railway" title="Standard-gauge railway">standard-gauge</a>. All stations have escalators, lifts, and tactile tiles to guide the visually impaired from station entrances to trains. There are 18 designated parking sites at Metro stations to further encourage the use of the system. In March 2010, DMRC partnered with Google India (through Google Transit) to provide train schedule and route information to mobile devices with Google Maps.
It has a combination of elevated, at-grade, and underground lines, and uses both broad gauge and standard gauge rolling stock. Four types of rolling stock are used: Mitsubishi–ROTEM Broad gauge, Bombardier MOVIA, Mitsubishi–ROTEM Standard gauge, and CAF Beasain Standard gauge. The Phase-I of Delhi Metro was built for US$2.3 billion and the Phase-II was expected to cost an additional <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>216 billion</span> (US$2.7 billion).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloomberg.com:_Opinion_190-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg.com:_Opinion-190">[188]</a></sup> Phase-II has a total length of 128 km and was completed by 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Economictimes.indiatimes.com_191-1"><a href="#cite_note-Economictimes.indiatimes.com-191">[189]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Metro" title="Delhi Metro">Delhi Metro</a> completed 10 years of operation on 25 December 2012. It carries millions of passengers every day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10_years_of_Delhi_Metro_192-1"><a href="#cite_note-10_years_of_Delhi_Metro-192">[190]</a></sup>
</p><p>Delhi Metro is being built and operated by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delhi_Metro_Rail_Corporation_Limited" title="Delhi Metro Rail Corporation Limited">Delhi Metro Rail Corporation Limited</a> (DMRC), a state-owned company with equal equity participation from the Government of India and the Government of the National Capital Territory of Delhi. However, the organization is under the administrative control of the Ministry of Urban Development, Government of India. Besides the construction and operation of the Delhi Metro, DMRC is also involved in the planning and implementation of metro rail, monorail, and high-speed rail projects in India and providing consultancy services to other metro projects in the country as well as abroad. The Delhi Metro project was spearheaded by <a href="/wiki/Padma_Vibhushan" title="Padma Vibhushan">Padma Vibhushan</a> <a href="/wiki/E._Sreedharan" title="E. Sreedharan">E. Sreedharan</a>, the managing director of DMRC and popularly known as the "Metro Man" of India. He famously resigned from DMRC taking moral responsibility for a metro bridge collapse, which took five lives. Sreedharan was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Legion_of_Honour" title="Legion of Honour">Legion of Honour</a> by the French Government for his contribution to Delhi Metro.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[195]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Delhi" title="Ethnic groups in Delhi">Ethnic groups in Delhi</a></div>
<p>According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_census_of_India" title="2011 census of India">2011 census of India</a>, the population of NCT of Delhi is 16,753,235.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-censusindia1_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-censusindia1-200">[196]</a></sup> The corresponding population density was 11,297 persons per km<sup>2</sup> with a sex ratio of 866 women per 1000 men, and a literacy rate of 86.34%. In 2004, the birth rate, death rate and infant mortality rate per 1000 population were 20.03, 5.59 and 13.08, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecosurv3_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-ecosurv3-201">[197]</a></sup> In 2001, the population of Delhi increased by 285,000 as a result of migration and by 215,000 as a result of natural population growth,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecosurv3_201-1"><a href="#cite_note-ecosurv3-201">[197]</a></sup> which made Delhi one of the fastest-growing cities in the world. <a href="/wiki/Dwarka,_Delhi" title="Dwarka, Delhi">Dwarka Sub City</a>, Asia's largest planned residential area, is located within the National Capital Territory of Delhi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[198]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Urban_sprawl" title="Urban sprawl">Urban expansion</a> has resulted in Delhi's urban area now being considered as extending beyond the NCT boundaries to incorporate the towns and cities of neighbouring states including <a href="/wiki/Faridabad" title="Faridabad">Faridabad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gurgaon" title="Gurgaon">Gurgaon</a> of <a href="/wiki/Haryana" title="Haryana">Haryana</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ghaziabad" title="Ghaziabad">Ghaziabad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Noida" title="Noida">Noida</a> of <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a>, the total population of which is estimated by the United Nations at over 28 million. According to the UN this makes Delhi urban area the world's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_urban_areas_by_population" title="List of urban areas by population">second-largest</a>, after Tokyo,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNcities2018_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-UNcities2018-8">[8]</a></sup> although <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demographia" title="Demographia">Demographia</a> declares the <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a> urban area to be the second-largest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Demographia_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-Demographia-203">[199]</a></sup> The 2011 census provided two figures for urban area population: 16,314,838 within the NCT boundary,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Delhiuapop2011_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-Delhiuapop2011-204">[200]</a></sup> and 21,753,486 for the <i>Extended Urban Area</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pibmumbai1_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-pibmumbai1-205">[201]</a></sup> The 2021 regional plan released by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a> renamed the <i>Extended Urban Area</i> from <i>Delhi Metropolitan Area (DMA)</i> as defined by the 2001 plan<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DMA_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-DMA-206">[202]</a></sup> to <i><a href="/wiki/National_Capital_Region_(India)#Central_National_Capital_Region" title="National Capital Region (India)">Central National Capital Region</a> (CNCR)</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DMA_206-1"><a href="#cite_note-DMA-206">[202]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[203]</a></sup> Around 49% of the population of Delhi lives in slums and unauthorized colonies without any civic amenities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[204]</a></sup> The majority of the slums have inadequate provisions to the basic facilities and according to a DUSIB report, almost 22% of the people do open defecation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[205]</a></sup>
</p><p>Major social groups of Delhi include <a href="/wiki/Brahmin" title="Brahmin">Brahmins</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gujjar" title="Gujjar">Gujjars</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jat_people" title="Jat people">Jats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vaishya" title="Vaishya">Vaishyas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khatri" title="Khatri">Khatris</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rajputs" title="Rajputs">Rajputs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ahir" title="Ahir">Ahirs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Punjabis" title="Punjabis">Punjabis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Purvanchal" title="Purvanchal">Purvanchalis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bengalis" title="Bengalis">Bengalis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand" title="Uttarakhand">Uttarakhandis</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a>,  <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sikh" title="Sikh">Sikhs</a>, etc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[206]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[207]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[209]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-censusindia1_200-1"><a href="#cite_note-censusindia1-200">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[210]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[211]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 202.66666666667px"><div style="width: 202.66666666667px">

<div class="thumbcaption">
<p>Religions in delhi (2011)
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:darkorange; color:black;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> (81.68%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:green; color:white;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (12.86%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:darkkhaki; color:black;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a> (3.40%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Maroon; color:white;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a> (0.99%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:dodgerblue; color:black;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> (0.87%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Yellow; color:black;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> (0.11%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Grey; color:black;"> </span> Others (0.09%)</div>
</div>
</div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> is Delhi's predominant religious faith, with 81.68% of Delhi's population, followed by <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (12.86%), <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a> (3.40%), <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a> (0.99%), Christianity (0.87%), and <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> (0.11%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Religion_PCA_2011_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-Religion_PCA_2011-216">[212]</a></sup> Other minority religions include <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼísm</a> and Judaism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lonelyplanet_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lonelyplanet-217">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the 50th report of the commissioner for linguistic minorities in India, which was submitted in 2014, <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> is Delhi's most spoken language, with 80.94% speakers, followed by <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_language" title="Punjabi language">Punjabi</a> (7.14%), <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a> (6.31%) and <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a> (1.50%). 4.11% of the Delhites speak other languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-langminor_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-langminor-218">[214]</a></sup> Hindi is also the official language of Delhi while Urdu and Punjabi have been declared as additional official languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-langminor_218-1"><a href="#cite_note-langminor-218">[214]</a></sup> According to the Directorate of Education, <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Delhi" title="Government of Delhi">GNCTD</a> the following languages are taught in schools in Delhi under the <a href="/wiki/Three-language_formula" title="Three-language formula">three-language formula</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[215]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_India" title="Culture of India">Culture of India</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:392px;max-width:392px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:206px;max-width:206px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:135px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Traditional_pottery_in_Dilli_Haat.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="438" data-file-width="660" decoding="async" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Traditional_pottery_in_Dilli_Haat.jpg/204px-Traditional_pottery_in_Dilli_Haat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Traditional_pottery_in_Dilli_Haat.jpg/306px-Traditional_pottery_in_Dilli_Haat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Traditional_pottery_in_Dilli_Haat.jpg/408px-Traditional_pottery_in_Dilli_Haat.jpg 2x" width="204"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">Traditional pottery on display in <i><a href="/wiki/Dilli_Haat" title="Dilli Haat">Dilli Haat</a></i></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:135px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pragati_Maidan,_inside_hall_18_(3).JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Pragati_Maidan%2C_inside_hall_18_%283%29.JPG/180px-Pragati_Maidan%2C_inside_hall_18_%283%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Pragati_Maidan%2C_inside_hall_18_%283%29.JPG/270px-Pragati_Maidan%2C_inside_hall_18_%283%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Pragati_Maidan%2C_inside_hall_18_%283%29.JPG/360px-Pragati_Maidan%2C_inside_hall_18_%283%29.JPG 2x" width="180"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">Pragati Maidan hosts the <i>World Book Fair</i> biennially</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Delhi's culture has been influenced by its lengthy history and historic association as the capital of India. Although a strong <a href="/wiki/Punjabis" title="Punjabis">Punjabi</a> Influence can be seen in <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_language" title="Punjabi language">language</a>, <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_clothing" title="Punjabi clothing">Dress</a> and <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_cuisine" title="Punjabi cuisine">Cuisine</a> brought by the large number of refugees who came following the <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_India" title="Partition of India">partition in 1947</a> the recent migration from other parts of India has made it a <a href="/wiki/Melting_pot" title="Melting pot">melting pot</a>. This is exemplified by many significant monuments in the city. The <a href="/wiki/Archaeological_Survey_of_India" title="Archaeological Survey of India">Archaeological Survey of India</a> recognises 1,200 heritage buildings<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[216]</a></sup> and 175 monuments as national heritage sites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-asimonuments_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-asimonuments-221">[217]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the Old City, the Mughals and the Turkic rulers constructed several architecturally significant buildings, such as the <a href="/wiki/Jama_Masjid,_Delhi" title="Jama Masjid, Delhi">Jama Masjid</a>—India's largest mosque<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jama_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jama-222">[218]</a></sup> built in 1656<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[219]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Red_Fort" title="Red Fort">Red Fort</a>. Three <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a>—the Red Fort, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qutab_Minar" title="Qutab Minar">Qutub Minar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Humayun%27s_Tomb" title="Humayun's Tomb">Humayun's Tomb</a>—are located in Delhi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whsite_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-whsite-224">[220]</a></sup> Other monuments include the <a href="/wiki/India_Gate" title="India Gate">India Gate</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yantra_Mandir_(Delhi)" title="Yantra Mandir (Delhi)">Jantar Mantar</a>—an 18th-century astronomical observatory—and the <a href="/wiki/Purana_Qila" title="Purana Qila">Purana Qila</a>—a 16th-century fortress. The <a href="/wiki/Laxminarayan_Temple" title="Laxminarayan Temple">Laxminarayan Temple</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Akshardham_(Delhi)" title="Akshardham (Delhi)">Akshardham temple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gurudwara_Bangla_Sahib" title="Gurudwara Bangla Sahib">Gurudwara Bangla Sahib</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Temple" title="Lotus Temple">Lotus Temple</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISKCON_Temple_Delhi" title="ISKCON Temple Delhi">ISKCON temple</a> are examples of modern architecture. <a href="/wiki/Raj_Ghat_and_associated_memorials" title="Raj Ghat and associated memorials">Raj Ghat and associated memorials</a> houses memorials of <a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Mahatma Gandhi</a> and other notable personalities. New Delhi houses several government buildings and official residences reminiscent of British colonial architecture, including the Rashtrapati Bhavan, <a href="/wiki/Secretariat_Building,_New_Delhi" title="Secretariat Building, New Delhi">the Secretariat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rajpath" title="Rajpath">Rajpath</a>, the Parliament of India and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vijay_Chowk" title="Vijay Chowk">Vijay Chowk</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tomb_of_Safdar_Jang" title="Tomb of Safdar Jang">Safdarjung's Tomb</a> is an example of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mughal_gardens" title="Mughal gardens">Mughal gardens</a> style. Some regal <i>havelis</i> (palatial residences) are in the Old City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jacob_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-jacob-225">[221]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Temple" title="Lotus Temple">Lotus Temple</a> is a Baháʼí House of Worship completed in 1986. Notable for its flowerlike shape, it serves as the Mother Temple of the Indian subcontinent and has become a prominent attraction in the city. 
The <a href="/wiki/National_Museum,_New_Delhi" title="National Museum, New Delhi">National Museum</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Gallery_of_Modern_Art" title="National Gallery of Modern Art">National Gallery of Modern Art</a> are some of the largest museums in the country. Other museums in Delhi include the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Natural_History,_New_Delhi" title="National Museum of Natural History, New Delhi">National Museum of Natural History</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Rail_Museum,_New_Delhi" title="National Rail Museum, New Delhi">National Rail Museum</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Philatelic_Museum,_New_Delhi" title="National Philatelic Museum, New Delhi">National Philatelic Museum</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Chandni_Chowk" title="Chandni Chowk">Chandni Chowk</a>, a 17th-century market, is one of the most popular shopping areas in Delhi for jewellery and <i>Zari</i> <a href="/wiki/Sari" title="Sari">saris</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chandni_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chandni-226">[222]</a></sup> Delhi's arts and crafts include, <i><a href="/wiki/Zardozi" title="Zardozi">Zardozi</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[223]</a></sup>—an embroidery done with gold thread—<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[224]</a></sup> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meenakari" title="Meenakari">Meenakari</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[225]</a></sup>—the art of enamelling.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:392px;max-width:392px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:194px;max-width:194px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:128px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chhath_Puja_Sandya_Aragh-005.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Chhath_Puja_Sandya_Aragh-005.jpg/192px-Chhath_Puja_Sandya_Aragh-005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Chhath_Puja_Sandya_Aragh-005.jpg/288px-Chhath_Puja_Sandya_Aragh-005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Chhath_Puja_Sandya_Aragh-005.jpg/384px-Chhath_Puja_Sandya_Aragh-005.jpg 2x" width="192"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">More than a quarter of the immigrants in Delhi are from <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a> and neighboring states. <a href="/wiki/Chhath" title="Chhath">Chhath</a>, a festival of rural Bihar is now popular in Delhi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kapur-busstand-chhath_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-kapur-busstand-chhath-230">[226]</a></sup></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:194px;max-width:194px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:128px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Basant_Celebrations_at_Dargah.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="534" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Basant_Celebrations_at_Dargah.jpg/192px-Basant_Celebrations_at_Dargah.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Basant_Celebrations_at_Dargah.jpg/288px-Basant_Celebrations_at_Dargah.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Basant_Celebrations_at_Dargah.jpg/384px-Basant_Celebrations_at_Dargah.jpg 2x" width="192"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">On <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basant_Panchmi" title="Basant Panchmi">Basant Panchmi</a> eve, <a href="/wiki/Qawwali" title="Qawwali">qawwali</a> singers wearing yellow headbands gather at the <a href="/wiki/Dargah" title="Dargah">dargah</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufi</a> saint <a href="/wiki/Nizamuddin_Auliya" title="Nizamuddin Auliya">Nizamuddin Auliya</a> to sing verses from <a href="/wiki/Amir_Khusrau" title="Amir Khusrau">Amir Khusrau</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tiwari-wire-auliya_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-tiwari-wire-auliya-231">[227]</a></sup></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Delhi's association and geographic proximity to the capital, New Delhi, has amplified the importance of national events and holidays like <a href="/wiki/Republic_Day_(India)" title="Republic Day (India)">Republic Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(India)" title="Independence Day (India)">Independence Day</a> (15 August) and <i><a href="/wiki/Gandhi_Jayanti" title="Gandhi Jayanti">Gandhi Jayanti</a></i>. On Independence Day, the Prime Minister addresses the nation from the Red Fort. The <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Republic_Day_parade" title="Delhi Republic Day parade">Republic Day Parade</a> is a large cultural and military parade showcasing India's cultural diversity and military strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-repmil_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-repmil-232">[228]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-repcul_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-repcul-233">[229]</a></sup> Over the centuries, Delhi has become known for its composite culture, and a festival that symbolises this is the <i><a href="/wiki/Phool_Walon_Ki_Sair" title="Phool Walon Ki Sair">Phool Walon Ki Sair</a></i>, which takes place in September. Flowers and <i>pankhe</i>—fans embroidered with flowers—are offered to the shrine of the 13th-century Sufi saint <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khwaja_Bakhtiyar_Kaki" title="Khwaja Bakhtiyar Kaki">Khwaja Bakhtiyar Kaki</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Yogmaya_Temple" title="Yogmaya Temple">Yogmaya Temple</a>, both situated in <a href="/wiki/Mehrauli" title="Mehrauli">Mehrauli</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[230]</a></sup>
</p><p>Religious festivals include <i><a href="/wiki/Diwali" title="Diwali">Diwali</a></i> (the festival of lights), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahavir_Jayanti" title="Mahavir Jayanti">Mahavir Jayanti</a></i>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guru_Nanak%27s_Birthday" title="Guru Nanak's Birthday">Guru Nanak's Birthday</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Raksha_Bandhan" title="Raksha Bandhan">Raksha Bandhan</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Durga_Puja" title="Durga Puja">Durga Puja</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Holi" title="Holi">Holi</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lohri" title="Lohri">Lohri</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Chauth" title="Chauth">Chauth</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Krishna_Janmastami" title="Krishna Janmastami">Krishna Janmastami</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maha_Shivratri" title="Maha Shivratri">Maha Shivratri</a></i>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eid_ul-Fitr" title="Eid ul-Fitr">Eid ul-Fitr</a>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Day_of_Ashura" title="Day of Ashura">Moharram</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddha_Jayanti" title="Buddha Jayanti">Buddha Jayanti</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-repcul_233-1"><a href="#cite_note-repcul-233">[229]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Qutub_Festival" title="Qutub Festival">Qutub Festival</a> is a cultural event during which performances of musicians and dancers from all over India are showcased at night, with the Qutub Minar as a backdrop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-qutubfest_235-0"><a href="#cite_note-qutubfest-235">[231]</a></sup> Other events such as Kite Flying Festival, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Mango_Festival,_Delhi" title="International Mango Festival, Delhi">International Mango Festival</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Vasant_Panchami" title="Vasant Panchami">Vasant Panchami</a></i> (the Spring Festival) are held every year in Delhi. The <a href="/wiki/Auto_Expo" title="Auto Expo">Auto Expo</a>, Asia's largest auto show,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-236">[232]</a></sup> is held in Delhi biennially. The <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi_World_Book_Fair" title="New Delhi World Book Fair">New Delhi World Book Fair</a>, held biennially at the <a href="/wiki/Pragati_Maidan" title="Pragati Maidan">Pragati Maidan</a>, is the second-largest exhibition of books in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indiatimes1_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-indiatimes1-237">[233]</a></sup> Delhi is often regarded as the "Book Capital" of India because of high readership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[234]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/India_International_Trade_Fair" title="India International Trade Fair">India International Trade Fair</a> (IITF), organised by <a href="/wiki/India_Trade_Promotion_Organisation" title="India Trade Promotion Organisation">ITPO</a> is the biggest cultural and shopping fair of Delhi which takes place in November each year and is visited by more than 1.5 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[235]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Indian_cuisine" title="Indian cuisine">Indian cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Karim%27s_Hotel,_Delhi(4).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="2448" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Karim%27s_Hotel%2C_Delhi%284%29.jpg/220px-Karim%27s_Hotel%2C_Delhi%284%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Karim%27s_Hotel%2C_Delhi%284%29.jpg/330px-Karim%27s_Hotel%2C_Delhi%284%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Karim%27s_Hotel%2C_Delhi%284%29.jpg/440px-Karim%27s_Hotel%2C_Delhi%284%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Karim%27s_Hotel,_Delhi(4).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kitchen, <a href="/wiki/Karim%27s" title="Karim's">Karim's</a>, Old Delhi, a historic <a href="/wiki/Restaurant" title="Restaurant">restaurant</a>, estab. 1913.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[236]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>As India's national capital and centuries old <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mughal_empire" title="Mughal empire">Mughal</a> capital, Delhi influenced the food habits of its residents and is where <a href="/wiki/Mughlai_cuisine" title="Mughlai cuisine">Mughlai cuisine</a> originated. Along with Indian cuisine, a variety of international cuisines are popular among the residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Narayan_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-Narayan-241">[237]</a></sup> The dearth of food habits among the city's residents created a unique style of cooking which became popular throughout the world, with dishes such as <i><a href="/wiki/Kebab" title="Kebab">Kebab</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Biryani" title="Biryani">biryani</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Tandoor" title="Tandoor">tandoori</a></i>. The city's classic dishes include <a href="/wiki/Butter_chicken" title="Butter chicken">butter chicken</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dal_makhani" title="Dal makhani">dal makhani</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Shahi_paneer" title="Shahi paneer">shahi paneer</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aloo_chaat" title="Aloo chaat">aloo chaat</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Chaat" title="Chaat">chaat</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dahi_bhalla" title="Dahi bhalla">dahi bhalla</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Kachori" title="Kachori">kachori</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Panipuri" title="Panipuri">gol gappe</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Samosa" title="Samosa">samosa</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Chole_bhature" title="Chole bhature">chole bhature</a></i>, <i>chole kulche</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Gulab_jamun" title="Gulab jamun">gulab jamun</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Jalebi" title="Jalebi">jalebi</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Lassi" title="Lassi">lassi</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Narayan_241-1"><a href="#cite_note-Narayan-241">[237]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-commonwealth_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-commonwealth-242">[238]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 40–50, 189–196">: 40–50, 189–196 </span></sup>
</p><p>The fast living habits of Delhi's people has motivated the growth of <a href="/wiki/Street_food" title="Street food">street food</a> outlets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-commonwealth_242-1"><a href="#cite_note-commonwealth-242">[238]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 41">: 41 </span></sup> A trend of dining at local <i><a href="/wiki/Dhaba" title="Dhaba">dhabas</a></i> is popular among the residents. High-profile restaurants have gained popularity in recent years, among the popular restaurants are the Karim Hotel, the Punjab Grill and Bukhara.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-243">[239]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Gali_Paranthe_Wali" title="Gali Paranthe Wali">Gali Paranthe Wali</a></i> (the street of fried bread) is a street in Chandni Chowk particularly for food eateries since the 1870s. Almost the entire street is occupied by fast food stalls or <a href="/wiki/Hawker_(trade)" title="Hawker (trade)">street vendors</a>. It has nearly become a tradition that almost every prime minister of India has visited the street to eat <i><a href="/wiki/Paratha" title="Paratha">paratha</a></i> at least once. Other Indian cuisines are also available in this area even though the street specialises in north Indian food.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-commonwealth_242-2"><a href="#cite_note-commonwealth-242">[238]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 40–50">: 40–50 </span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[240]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Delhi" title="Education in Delhi">Education in Delhi</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Delhi" title="List of schools in Delhi">List of schools in Delhi</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" pharmacy,1921.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:128px;max-width:128px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:85px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" A. Ansari">M. A. Ansari</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zakir_Hussain_(politician)" title="Zakir Hussain (politician)">Zakir Hussain</a>.</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:128px;max-width:128px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:94px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Delhiuni.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Delhiuni.jpg/126px-Delhiuni.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Delhiuni.jpg/189px-Delhiuni.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Delhiuni.jpg/252px-Delhiuni.jpg 2x" width="126"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Delhi" title="University of Delhi">University of Delhi</a> was founded in 1922. title="Vice-chancellor">vice-chancellor</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:130px;max-width:130px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:94px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anglo_Arabic_School%27s_Hostel_earlier_known_as_Ghaziuddin_Khan_Madrasa.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2875" data-file-width="3893" decoding="async" height="95"
