srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Anglo_Arabic_School%27s_Hostel_earlier_known_as_Ghaziuddin_Khan_Madrasa.jpg/192px-Anglo_Arabic_School%27s_Hostel_earlier_known_as_Ghaziuddin_Khan_Madrasa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Anglo_Arabic_School%27s_Hostel_earlier_known_as_Ghaziuddin_Khan_Madrasa.jpg/256px-Anglo_Arabic_School%27s_Hostel_earlier_known_as_Ghaziuddin_Khan_Madrasa.jpg 2x" width="128"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center"><a href="/wiki/Dormitory" title="Dormitory">Dormitory</a> of <a href="/wiki/Anglo_Arabic_Senior_Secondary_School" title="Anglo Arabic Senior Secondary School">Anglo Arabic Senior Secondary School</a>, founded 1696, reorganized 1828.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:128px;max-width:128px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:94px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Delhi_Government_School_Student_defining_Happiness_in_Happiness_Class.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3024" data-file-width="4032" decoding="async" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Delhi_Government_School_Student_defining_Happiness_in_Happiness_Class.jpg/126px-Delhi_Government_School_Student_defining_Happiness_in_Happiness_Class.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Delhi_Government_School_Student_defining_Happiness_in_Happiness_Class.jpg/189px-Delhi_Government_School_Student_defining_Happiness_in_Happiness_Class.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Delhi_Government_School_Student_defining_Happiness_in_Happiness_Class.jpg/252px-Delhi_Government_School_Student_defining_Happiness_in_Happiness_Class.jpg 2x" width="126"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">A Delhi government school student writing down the names of fruits and vegetables.</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Private schools in Delhi—which use either English or Hindi as the language of instruction—are affiliated to one of three administering bodies, the <a href="/wiki/Council_for_the_Indian_School_Certificate_Examinations" title="Council for the Indian School Certificate Examinations">Council for the Indian School Certificate Examinations</a> (CISCE), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Board_for_Secondary_Education" title="Central Board for Secondary Education">Central Board for Secondary Education</a> (CBSE)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[241]</a></sup> or the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Open_Schooling" title="National Institute of Open Schooling">National Institute of Open Schooling</a> (NIOS). In 2004–05, approximately 1,529,000 students were enrolled in primary schools, 822,000 in middle schools and 669,000 in secondary schools across Delhi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecosurv15_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-ecosurv15-246">[242]</a></sup> Female students represented 49% of the total enrolment. The same year, the Delhi government spent between 1.58% and 1.95% of its gross state domestic product on education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecosurv15_246-1"><a href="#cite_note-ecosurv15-246">[242]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/School#India" title="School">Schools</a> and higher educational institutions in Delhi are administered either by the <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Directorate_of_Education" title="Delhi Directorate of Education">Directorate of Education</a>, the NCT government or private organisations. In 2006, Delhi had 165 colleges, five medical colleges and eight engineering colleges,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecosurv15_246-2"><a href="#cite_note-ecosurv15-246">[242]</a></sup> seven major universities and nine <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deemed_University" title="Deemed University">deemed universities</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecosurv15_246-3"><a href="#cite_note-ecosurv15-246">[242]</a></sup>
</p><p>The premier management colleges of Delhi such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faculty_of_Management_Studies_(Delhi)" title="Faculty of Management Studies (Delhi)">Faculty of Management Studies (Delhi)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Foreign_Trade" title="Indian Institute of Foreign Trade">Indian Institute of Foreign Trade</a> rank the best in India. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/All_India_Institute_of_Medical_Sciences_Delhi" title="All India Institute of Medical Sciences Delhi">All India Institute of Medical Sciences Delhi</a> is a premier medical school for treatment and research. <a href="/wiki/National_Law_University,_Delhi" title="National Law University, Delhi">National Law University, Delhi</a> is a prominent law school and is affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Bar_Council_of_India" title="Bar Council of India">Bar Council of India</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Technology,_Delhi" title="Indian Institute of Technology, Delhi">Indian Institute of Technology, Delhi</a> situated in <a href="/wiki/Hauz_Khas" title="Hauz Khas">Hauz Khas</a> is a premier engineering college of India and ranks as one of the top institutes in South Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[243]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[244]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Delhi_Technological_University" title="Delhi Technological University">Delhi Technological University</a> (formerly Delhi College of Engineering), <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi_Delhi_Technical_University_for_Women" title="Indira Gandhi Delhi Technical University for Women">Indira Gandhi Delhi Technical University for Women</a> (formerly Indira Gandhi Institute of Technology), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indraprastha_Institute_of_Information_Technology" title="Indraprastha Institute of Information Technology">Indraprastha Institute of Information Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netaji_Subhas_University_of_Technology" title="Netaji Subhas University of Technology">Netaji Subhas University of Technology</a> (formerly Netaji Subhas Institute of Technology), <a href="/wiki/Guru_Gobind_Singh_Indraprastha_University" title="Guru Gobind Singh Indraprastha University">Guru Gobind Singh Indraprastha University</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Law_University" title="National Law University">National Law University</a>, Delhi are the only state universities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[245]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[246]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Delhi" title="University of Delhi">University of Delhi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru_University,_Delhi" title="Jawaharlal Nehru University, Delhi">Jawaharlal Nehru University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jamia_Millia_Islamia" title="Jamia Millia Islamia">Jamia Millia Islamia</a> are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_University_(India)" title="Central University (India)">central universities</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi_National_Open_University" title="Indira Gandhi National Open University">Indira Gandhi National Open University</a> is for <a href="/wiki/Distance_education" title="Distance education">distance education</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Act_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-Act-251">[247]</a></sup>
As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Delhi&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, about 16% of all Delhi residents possessed at least a college graduate degree.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[248]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_India" title="Media of India">Media of India</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pitampura_TV_Tower,_Delhi,_India.jpg"><img alt="Pitampura TV Tower with background of blue sky" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="686" data-file-width="514" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Pitampura_TV_Tower%2C_Delhi%2C_India.jpg/170px-Pitampura_TV_Tower%2C_Delhi%2C_India.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Pitampura_TV_Tower%2C_Delhi%2C_India.jpg/255px-Pitampura_TV_Tower%2C_Delhi%2C_India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Pitampura_TV_Tower%2C_Delhi%2C_India.jpg/340px-Pitampura_TV_Tower%2C_Delhi%2C_India.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pitampura_TV_Tower,_Delhi,_India.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pitampura_TV_Tower" title="Pitampura TV Tower">Pitampura TV Tower</a> broadcasts to Delhi</div></div></div>
<p>As the capital of India, Delhi is the focus of political reportage, including regular television broadcasts of Parliament sessions. Many national media agencies, including the state-owned <a href="/wiki/Press_Trust_of_India" title="Press Trust of India">Press Trust of India</a>, Media Trust of India and <a href="/wiki/Doordarshan" title="Doordarshan">Doordarshan</a>, are based in the city. Television programming includes two free terrestrial television channels offered by Doordarshan, and several Hindi, English, and regional-language <a href="/wiki/Cable_television" title="Cable television">cable</a> channels offered by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multi_system_operator" title="Multi system operator">multi system operators</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct_broadcast_satellite" title="Direct broadcast satellite">Satellite television</a> has yet to gain a large number of subscribers in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dthrediff_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-dthrediff-253">[249]</a></sup>
</p><p>Print journalism remains a popular news medium in Delhi. The city's Hindi newspapers include <i><a href="/wiki/Navbharat_Times" title="Navbharat Times">Navbharat Times</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindustan_Dainik" title="Hindustan Dainik">Hindustan Dainik</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Punjab_Kesari" title="Punjab Kesari">Punjab Kesari</a></i>, <i>Pavitra Bharat</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dainik_Jagran" title="Dainik Jagran">Dainik Jagran</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dainik_Bhaskar" title="Dainik Bhaskar">Dainik Bhaskar</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Amar_Ujala" title="Amar Ujala">Amar Ujala</a></i> and <i>Dainik Desbandhu</i>. Amongst the English language newspapers, the <i><a href="/wiki/Hindustan_Times" title="Hindustan Times">Hindustan Times</a></i>, with a daily circulation of over a million copies, is the single largest daily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[250]</a></sup> Other major English newspapers include <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times_of_India" title="The Times of India">The Times of India</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hindu" title="The Hindu">The Hindu</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_Express" title="Indian Express">Indian Express</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Business_Standard" title="Business Standard">Business Standard</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Pioneer_(daily)" title="The Pioneer (daily)">The Pioneer</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Statesman_(India)" title="The Statesman (India)">The Statesman</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Asian_Age" title="The Asian Age">The Asian Age</a></i>. Regional language newspapers include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malayalam_language" title="Malayalam language">Malayalam</a> daily <i><a href="/wiki/Malayala_Manorama" title="Malayala Manorama">Malayala Manorama</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a> dailies <i><a href="/wiki/Dinamalar" title="Dinamalar">Dinamalar</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Dinakaran" title="Dinakaran">Dinakaran</a></i>.
</p><p>Radio is a less popular mass medium in Delhi, although <a href="/wiki/Frequency_modulation" title="Frequency modulation">FM</a> radio has gained popularity<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-radiomass_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-radiomass-255">[251]</a></sup> since the inauguration of several new stations in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-asiawaves_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-asiawaves-256">[252]</a></sup>
A number of state-owned and private radio stations broadcast from Delhi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[253]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[254]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sports_in_Delhi" title="Sports in Delhi">Sports in Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/1951_Asian_Games" title="1951 Asian Games">1951 Asian Games</a>, <a href="/wiki/1982_Asian_Games" title="1982 Asian Games">1982 Asian Games</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2010_Commonwealth_Games" title="2010 Commonwealth Games">2010 Commonwealth Games</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_India" title="Culture of India">Culture of India</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:392px;max-width:392px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:203px;max-width:203px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:121px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Indian_athletes_at_the_First_Asiad.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="304" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Indian_athletes_at_the_First_Asiad.png/201px-Indian_athletes_at_the_First_Asiad.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Indian_athletes_at_the_First_Asiad.png/302px-Indian_athletes_at_the_First_Asiad.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Indian_athletes_at_the_First_Asiad.png/402px-Indian_athletes_at_the_First_Asiad.png 2x" width="201"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">Indian athletes marching into the <a href="/wiki/Major_Dhyan_Chand_National_Stadium" title="Major Dhyan Chand National Stadium">National Stadium</a> during the opening ceremony of the <a href="/wiki/1951_Asian_Games" title="1951 Asian Games">1951 Asian Games</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:185px;max-width:185px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:121px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jawaharlal_Nehru_Stadium_CWG_opening_ceremony.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3434" data-file-width="5161" decoding="async" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Jawaharlal_Nehru_Stadium_CWG_opening_ceremony.jpg/183px-Jawaharlal_Nehru_Stadium_CWG_opening_ceremony.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Jawaharlal_Nehru_Stadium_CWG_opening_ceremony.jpg/275px-Jawaharlal_Nehru_Stadium_CWG_opening_ceremony.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Jawaharlal_Nehru_Stadium_CWG_opening_ceremony.jpg/366px-Jawaharlal_Nehru_Stadium_CWG_opening_ceremony.jpg 2x" width="183"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru_Stadium,_Delhi" title="Jawaharlal Nehru Stadium, Delhi">Jawaharlal Nehru Stadium</a> on the night of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Commonwealth_Games" title="2010 Commonwealth Games">2010 Commonwealth Games</a> opening ceremony</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Delhi hosted the first Asian Games in 1951 from 4 to 11 March. A total of 489 athletes representing 11 Asian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Olympic_Committees" title="National Olympic Committees">National Olympic Committees</a> participated in 57 events from eight <a href="/wiki/Asian_Games_sports" title="Asian Games sports">sports and discipline</a>. The Games was the successor of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Far_Eastern_Games" title="Far Eastern Games">Far Eastern Games</a> and the revival of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Asiatic_Games" title="Western Asiatic Games">Western Asiatic Games</a>. On 13 February 1949, the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Games_Federation" title="Asian Games Federation">Asian Games Federation</a> was formally established in Delhi, with Delhi unanimously announced as the first host city of the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Games" title="Asian Games">Asian Games</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dhyan_Chand_National_Stadium" title="Dhyan Chand National Stadium">National Stadium</a> was the venue for all events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[255]</a></sup> Over 40,000 spectators watched the opening ceremony of the Games in National Stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[256]</a></sup>
</p><p>Delhi hosted the ninth Asian Games for the second time in 1982 from 19 November to 4 December. This was the second time the city has hosted the Asian Games and was also the first Asian Games to be held under the aegis of the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Council_of_Asia" title="Olympic Council of Asia">Olympic Council of Asia</a>. A total of 3,411 athletes from 33 <a href="/wiki/National_Olympic_Committee" title="National Olympic Committee">National Olympic Committees</a> participated in these games, competing in 196 events in 21 sports and 23 disciplines.  The <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru_Stadium_(Delhi)" title="Jawaharlal Nehru Stadium (Delhi)">Jawaharlal Nehru Stadium</a>, which has a capacity of 60,000 people, was built purposely for the event and hosted its opening ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[257]</a></sup>
</p><p>Delhi hosted the <a href="/wiki/2010_Commonwealth_Games" title="2010 Commonwealth Games">Nineteenth Commonwealth Games</a> in 2010, which ran from 3 to 14 October and was the largest sporting event held in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[258]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[259]</a></sup> The opening ceremony of the 2010 Commonwealth Games was held at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru_Stadium,_Delhi" title="Jawaharlal Nehru Stadium, Delhi">Jawaharlal Nehru Stadium</a>, the main stadium of the event, in New Delhi at 7:00 pm <a href="/wiki/Indian_Standard_Time" title="Indian Standard Time">Indian Standard Time</a> on 3 October 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[260]</a></sup> The ceremony featured over 8,000 performers and lasted for two and a half hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[261]</a></sup> It is estimated that <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>3.5 billion</span> (US$44 million) were spent to produce the ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[262]</a></sup> Events took place at 12 competition venues. 20 training venues were used in the Games, including seven venues within <a href="/wiki/Delhi_University" title="Delhi University">Delhi University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Non-Competition_Venues_267-0"><a href="#cite_note-Non-Competition_Venues-267">[263]</a></sup> The rugby stadium in Delhi University North Campus hosted rugby games for Commonwealth Games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Non-Competition_Venues_267-1"><a href="#cite_note-Non-Competition_Venues-267">[263]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> and <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> are the most popular sports in Delhi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popular_268-0"><a href="#cite_note-popular-268">[264]</a></sup> There are several cricket grounds, or <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/meidan" title="wikt:meidan">maidans</a></i>, located across the city. The <a href="/wiki/Arun_Jaitley_Stadium" title="Arun Jaitley Stadium">Arun Jaitley Stadium</a> (known commonly as the <i>Kotla</i>) is one of the oldest cricket grounds in India and is a venue for international cricket matches. It is the home ground of the <a href="/wiki/Delhi_cricket_team" title="Delhi cricket team">Delhi cricket team</a>, which represents the city in the <a href="/wiki/Ranji_Trophy" title="Ranji Trophy">Ranji Trophy</a>, the premier Indian domestic <a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket" title="First-class cricket">first-class cricket</a> championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ranji_269-0"><a href="#cite_note-ranji-269">[265]</a></sup> The Delhi cricket team has produced several world-class international cricketers such as <a href="/wiki/Virender_Sehwag" title="Virender Sehwag">Virender Sehwag</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virat_Kohli" title="Virat Kohli">Virat Kohli</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[266]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gautam_Gambhir" title="Gautam Gambhir">Gautam Gambhir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madan_Lal" title="Madan Lal">Madan Lal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chetan_Chauhan" title="Chetan Chauhan">Chetan Chauhan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shikhar_Dhawan" title="Shikhar Dhawan">Shikhar Dhawan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ishant_Sharma" title="Ishant Sharma">Ishant Sharma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manoj_Prabhakar" title="Manoj Prabhakar">Manoj Prabhakar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bishan_Singh_Bedi" title="Bishan Singh Bedi">Bishan Singh Bedi</a> to name a few. The <a href="/wiki/Railways_cricket_team" title="Railways cricket team">Railways</a> and <a href="/wiki/Services_cricket_team" title="Services cricket team">Services</a> cricket teams in the Ranji Trophy also play their home matches in Delhi, in the <a href="/wiki/Karnail_Singh_Stadium" title="Karnail Singh Stadium">Karnail Singh Stadium</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Harbax_Singh_Stadium" title="Harbax Singh Stadium">Harbax Singh Stadium</a>, respectively.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The city is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Premier_League" title="Indian Premier League">Indian Premier League</a> team <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Capitals" title="Delhi Capitals">Delhi Capitals</a>, who play their home matches at the Kotla.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ambedkar_Stadium" title="Ambedkar Stadium">Ambedkar Stadium</a>, a football stadium in Delhi which holds 21,000 people, was the venue for the Indian football team's World Cup qualifier against UAE on 28 July 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[267]</a></sup> Delhi hosted the Nehru Cup in <a href="/wiki/2007_Nehru_Cup" title="2007 Nehru Cup">2007</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[268]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/2009_Nehru_Cup" title="2009 Nehru Cup">2009</a>, in both of which India defeated <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> 1–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[269]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Elite_Football_League_of_India" title="Elite Football League of India">Elite Football League of India</a>, Delhi's first professional <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> franchise, the <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Defenders" title="Delhi Defenders">Delhi Defenders</a> played its first season in <a href="/wiki/Pune" title="Pune">Pune</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[270]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Buddh_International_Circuit" title="Buddh International Circuit">Buddh International Circuit</a> in Greater Noida, a suburb of Delhi, formerly hosted the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Formula_1" title="Formula 1">Formula 1</a> <a href="/wiki/Indian_Grand_Prix" title="Indian Grand Prix">Indian Grand Prix</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[271]</a></sup>
</p>

<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">(<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <small>Hindi pronunciation: </small><span class="IPA" lang="hi-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Hindi_and_Urdu" title="Help:IPA/Hindi and Urdu">[ˈdɪlːiː]</a></span> <i>dillī</i>; <small>Punjabi pronunciation: </small><span class="IPA" lang="pa-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Punjabi" title="Help:IPA/Punjabi">[ˈdɪlːiː]</a></span> <i>dillī</i>; <small>Urdu pronunciation: </small><span class="IPA" lang="ur-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Hindi_and_Urdu" title="Help:IPA/Hindi and Urdu">[ˈdeɦliː]</a></span> <i>dêhlī</i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-habib,_Royal,_karamchandani,_National_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-habib,_Royal,_karamchandani,_National-13">[13]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-173"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-173">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The elevated Delhi metro is seen above in <a href="/wiki/Azadpur" title="Azadpur">Azadpur</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cities.expressindia.com_127-2"><a href="#cite_note-cities.expressindia.com-127">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-fn1-197"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-fn1_197-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Transfer stations are counted more than once. There are 24 transfer stations. If transfer stations are counted only once, the result will be 230 stations. <a href="/wiki/Ashok_Park_Main_metro_station" title="Ashok Park Main metro station">Ashok Park Main</a> station, where the two diverging branches of <a href="/wiki/Green_Line_(Delhi_Metro)" title="Green Line (Delhi Metro)">Green Line</a> share tracks/platforms, is anyway counted as a single station. Stations of <a href="/wiki/Aqua_Line_(Noida_Metro)" title="Aqua Line (Noida Metro)">Noida Metro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rapid_Metro_Gurgaon" title="Rapid Metro Gurgaon">Gurgaon Metro</a> are not counted. If stations of <a href="/wiki/Aqua_Line_(Noida_Metro)" title="Aqua Line (Noida Metro)">Noida Metro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rapid_Metro_Gurgaon" title="Rapid Metro Gurgaon">Gurgaon Metro</a> are counted, the result will be 286 stations<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-route_map_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-route_map-195">[193]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-present_network_194-1"><a href="#cite_note-present_network-194">[192]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-introduction_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-introduction-196">[194]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-fn2-198"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-fn2_198-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The total length of Delhi Metro is 348.12 kilometres (216.31 mi). The operations &amp; maintenance of <a href="/wiki/Rapid_Metro_Gurgaon" title="Rapid Metro Gurgaon">Gurgaon Metro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Noida_Metro" title="Noida Metro">Noida Metro</a> is currently undertaken by <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Metro_Rail_Corporation" title="Delhi Metro Rail Corporation">DMRC</a>, so the total length operated by DMRC is 390.14 kilometres (242.42 mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-route_map_195-1"><a href="#cite_note-route_map-195">[193]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-introduction_196-1"><a href="#cite_note-introduction-196">[194]</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-talbot-singh-delhi-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-talbot-singh-delhi_16-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFTalbotSingh2009">Talbot, Ian; Singh, Gurharpal (2009), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=utKmPQAACAAJ&amp;pg=PA118" rel="nofollow"><i>The Partition of India</i></a>, Cambridge University Press, pp. 118–119, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-521-85661-4" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-521-85661-4"><bdi>978-0-521-85661-4</bdi></a>, <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20211202201454/https://books.google.com/books?id=utKmPQAACAAJ&amp;pg=PA118" rel="nofollow">archived</a> from the original on 2 December 2021<span class="reference-accessdate">, retrieved <span class="nowrap">3 December</span> 2021</span>, <q>It is now almost a cliché that the Partition transformed Delhi from a Mughal to a Punjabi city.  The bitter experiences of the refugees encouraged them to support right-wing Hindu parties. ... Trouble began in September (1947) after the arrival of refugees from Pakistan who were determined on revenge and driving Muslims out of properties which they could then occupy.  Gandhi in his prayer meetings in Birla House denounced the 'crooked and ungentlemanly' squeezing out of Muslims.  Despite these exhortations, two-thirds of the city's Muslims were to eventually abandon India's capital.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Partition+of+India&amp;rft.pages=118-119&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-521-85661-4&amp;rft.aulast=Talbot&amp;rft.aufirst=Ian&amp;rft.au=Singh%2C+Gurharpal&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DutKmPQAACAAJ%26pg%3DPA118&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ADelhi"></span></span>

October 2002. <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060522201305/https://portal.unesco.org/en/ev.php-URL_ID%3D6643%26URL_DO%3DDO_TOPIC%26URL_SECTION%3D201.html" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> from the original on 22 May 2006<span class="reference-accessdate">. <li id="cite_note-mcclary-medieval-monuments-37"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-mcclary-medieval-monuments_37-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFMcClary2020">McClary, Richard Piran (2020), <i>Medieval Monuments of Central Asia: Qarakhanid Architecture of the 11th and 12th Centuries</i>, Edinburgh University Press, p. 287, <q>The second story of the minaret, built during the reign of Iltutmish" (r. 1211-36), features a similar form of ribbing to the shaft as is seen at the Jar Kurgan minaret, but the lower section features alternating flanges and ribs, while the third storey is entirely flanged, with a stellate plan. The Qutb Minar is more closely related to the Ghaznavid and Ghurid traditions of minaret construction, although all the surviving large minarets from Central Asia can be seen to share certain general characteristics, namely, a tall tapering shaft and bands of decoration.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Medieval+Monuments+of+Central+Asia%3A+Qarakhanid+Architecture+of+the+11th+and+12th+Centuries&amp;rft.pages=287&amp;rft.pub=Edinburgh+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2020&amp;rft.aulast=McClary&amp;rft.aufirst=Richard+Piran&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ADelhi"></span></span>

Since the riots broke out in Delhi at the end of February, the worst religious conflict to engulf the capital in decades, questions have persisted about the role that the Delhi police played in enabling the violence, which was predominately Hindu mobs attacking Muslims.
